  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186074706" />
    <a title="Lisa Reads &amp; Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5395843-lisa-reads-reviews"><img alt="Lisa Reads &amp; Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515984298p2/5395843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186074706?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Reads &amp; Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Reads &amp; Reviews" href="/user/show/5395843-lisa-reads-reviews">Lisa Reads &amp; Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10860066-retribution-falls">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Firefly fans, space sci-fi adventure lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5395843-lisa-reads-reviews?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5395843-lisa-reads-reviews?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186074706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11897575794449130223">I'm a Firefly fan who picked up Retribution Falls to feed my nostalgia for good old cowboy/pirate steampunk westerns. I wasn't disappointed, to say the least. I laughed, got misty, and turned pages, completely absorbed in the adventure. The writing is excellent, the characters fleshy and fascinating (except for 2 by my count), and the plot is somewhat classic, yet it delivers startling breezes of fresh air, plenty enough to prohibit yawns. The next book, Black Lung Captain, is now on my to-read </span>
  <span id="freeText11897575794449130223" style="display:none">I'm a Firefly fan who picked up Retribution Falls to feed my nostalgia for good old cowboy/pirate steampunk westerns. I wasn't disappointed, to say the least. I laughed, got misty, and turned pages, completely absorbed in the adventure. The writing is excellent, the characters fleshy and fascinating (except for 2 by my count), and the plot is somewhat classic, yet it delivers startling breezes of fresh air, plenty enough to prohibit yawns. The next book, Black Lung Captain, is now on my to-read list. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575085169" href="/book/show/6854741-retribution-falls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21099598-derpa?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21099598-derpa?shelf=my-jam">my-jam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21099598-derpa?shelf=sidechars-of-awesome">sidechars-of-awesome</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287603621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12420573604932867642">Some people on here seem to give their 5 stars exclusively to books that supposedly change their lives and amounts awesome when mentioned in a serious conversation. There is nothing wrong with that, but I can't help just handing them out to books that were a fuckton of pure FUN in my opinion. This book is like that. Yes, you can say it's not the most original thing ever written by anyone, but I like to think of it as just... comfortably familiar, not boring and lamely cliché. What it does, it do</span>
  <span id="freeText12420573604932867642" style="display:none">Some people on here seem to give their 5 stars exclusively to books that supposedly change their lives and amounts awesome when mentioned in a serious conversation. There is nothing wrong with that, but I can't help just handing them out to books that were a fuckton of pure FUN in my opinion. This book is like that. Yes, you can say it's not the most original thing ever written by anyone, but I like to think of it as just... comfortably familiar, not boring and lamely cliché. What it does, it does well.<br />I have to point out that I've not seen Serenity (not really a sci-fi show fan, sorry), so <i>Retribution Falls</i> reminded me of anime instead, mostly Cowboy Bebop, Baccano!, with a tiny bit of FMA. The violence was stylized in a way that it really wasn't shocking or hard to read, and the same goes for all the angsty backstories of the characters. If you want something with plenty of action, without it being too too dark, this is a pretty safe bet in my opinion. <br />The characters are morally ambiguous enough to be kind of fun and honestly, I find them pretty much impossible to not like. My personal favourites were Crake (rich boy turned pirate because of a professional mistake) and Harkins (war veteran with a ton of issues). <br />Honestly, even though I have approximately 0 experience with steampunk, if it's like this, I think we will be good friends. Will definitely continue with the series, will recommend to my friends (aka throw it at their faces, sorry).<br />10/10, pure AWESOME</span>

<div id="review_3199025815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3199025815" />
    <a title="jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11030012-jade"><img alt="jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562419355p2/11030012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3199025815?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jade" href="/user/show/11030012-jade">jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10860066-retribution-falls">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of swashbuckling anti-hero adventures willing to overlook Bad Stereotypes</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to jade by: </span>
      many steampunk fans who shall remain anonymous
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=rogues-and-heists">rogues-and-heists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3199025815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13201730718602080176"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“ladies, gentlemen, we're out of here! your boss is upstairs, and only mildly wounded. go help him if you have the inclination. you'll also notice the house is on fire. make of that what you like.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>hello and welcome to the stage of darian frey, captain of the airship <s>Morally Grey</s>, I MEAN, the ketty jay!<br/><br/>the cover of this book promised me <b>gritty, arctic steampunk</b>. the blurb of this book and its glowing reviews promised me a dysfunctional, fucked-up airship crew with <b>dubious loyalties</b> wh</span>
  <span id="freeText13201730718602080176" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“ladies, gentlemen, we're out of here! your boss is upstairs, and only mildly wounded. go help him if you have the inclination. you'll also notice the house is on fire. make of that what you like.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />hello and welcome to the stage of darian frey, captain of the airship <s>Morally Grey</s>, I MEAN, the ketty jay!<br /><br />the cover of this book promised me <b>gritty, arctic steampunk</b>. the blurb of this book and its glowing reviews promised me a dysfunctional, fucked-up airship crew with <b>dubious loyalties</b> who dabble in piracy to escape their sordid <s>sad</s> pasts.<br /><br />so did it deliver on those promises? hell yes, it did.<br /><br />chris wooding was even kind enough to throw in swashbuckling duels, various pirate-cove-like towns and settlements, stunning aerial fights, and daemonic magic. it makes for a <b>fun adventure</b> story, albeit a bit predictable.<br /><br />you can definitely sense <b>its major inspirations</b>; a bit of the adventure and charming untrustworthiness of <i>pirates of the caribbean</i>, and a smidge of cool aircrafts and ragtag crews from the likes of <i>firefly</i> and <i>cowboy bebop</i>. as for the magic system, <i>fullmetal alchemist</i> comes to mind (including for plot reasons as well). <br /><br />in that same vein, its no-ruffles prose carries a very <b>visual, cinematic quality</b> that is a great contribution to its fighting scenes.<br /><br />with a book like this, half the fun is going to be watching the crew pull off whatever heist or con they’re involved in, as well as inevitably <b>grow closer and bond</b>. it took quite a while for that to take off, though: for the first half of the book, i remained in wait until the plot started properly accelerating and the backstories started dropping in.<br /><br />so what kind of characters can you expect?<br /><br /><b>frey</b> is the assholish, running-from-any-and-all-responsibilities captain. <b>silo</b> is the mysterious former-slave-now-engineer who barely says a word. <b>malvery</b> is the seemingly jolly, perpetually drunk ship’s doctor. <b>pinn</b> is the cocky, naive and crass fighter pilot. <b>harkins</b> is the jittery war veteran with an anxiety disorder.<br /><br />the newcomers are <b>crake</b>, a former-aristocrat-turned-passenger whose moral compass remains mostly intact, and <b>jez</b>, a competent navigator who swaps crews every few months. both of them have dark secrets to hide, and i loved them the most out of the whole bunch.<br /><br />the chapters hop and skip <b>between all of their perspectives</b>, but we spend most of our time with frey, crake, and jez. the switch between narrators and past/present wasn’t always clear cut, making for jarring moments where a new paragraph is suddenly from someone else’s perspective -- or that of the semi-omniscient narrator.<br /><br />in that same sense, this book could’ve used <b>more editing</b>. no doubt it would’ve helped smooth out those perspective and timeline shifts, as well as clean up some of the mistakes.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>however,</i>
</b> beyond a shadow of a doubt, my main gripe with this book was its latent sexism with a side-serving of homophobia. i say ‘latent’ even though it was pretty overt at times: consider that all female characters in this book get rated as either beautiful or ugly, with all the weird implications thereof (ugly women are super useful to have on your crew ’cause you won’t get distracted into fucking them!).<br /><br />and i’m just tired of this, okay? before someone makes the argument, <i>“jade, this is all written from womanizing male characters’ perspectives, it’s in-character that they think about women this way”</i> -- these beliefs are <b>never challenged</b>, and the narrative only seems to underline them.<br /><br />like, wooding uses the Tragic Rape Backstory trope to explain why a formerly beautiful, pure, sweet female character has now become “hardened, emotionless and ugly”. and after this whole tragedy unfolds, we then get to hear from the main character how he thinks her lips are painted a <i>“whorish red”</i> these days.<br /><br />i don’t even know how to unpack that. i really don’t! i feel like i’m just another clown in the circus. 🤡<br /><br />there’s also a couple of weird little <b>no homo moments</b>. oh, you don’t fuck a whore every night? ew, you must be One of Those. or consider this one for variety: yes, our main hero is so dashingly handsome all the ladies fall for him. as for the men? oh, he makes friends very easily! men just admire him!<br /><br /><i>[insert me wheezing in soulless laughter]</i><br /><br />(also, the only <b>character of color</b> on the crew is the escaped slave who is now utterly devoted to the white guy who saved his life. he rarely speaks, and when he does say something, wooding goes out of his way to write his accented speech phonetically so we can really get a feel for how Different he is. <i>mmmmMMM.</i>)<br /><br />undoubtedly, i would’ve rated this higher if the various -isms hadn’t gotten in the way. like, i’ll admit that right off the bat. but it was distracting, and it made a fun, fast-paced story that already employs a lot of tropes and stereotypes that much weaker for me.<br /><br />✎ <i>2.5 stars.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13201730718602080176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10495237081825674522" style="display:none">There was a lot to like in this book. Really it gets 3.5 stars rounded down. For about half the book, it would have been 4 stars. The world building was good. The fight scenes were great. It was a fast-paced action led story. The main protagonists were interesting.<br />Many other reviews said this was too similar to a TV show they had seen. Well, I hadn't seen it, but as the book developed, it sounded more and more like a TV episode. Also the author felt the need to explain to the reader how each character was feeling as the plot developed. It was annoying.<br />I enjoyed reading this but found myself skimming a bit towards the end. Not sure if I would continue with the series.</span>

<div id="review_584916890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/584916890" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/584916890?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345522511" href="/book/show/9063832-retribution-falls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584916890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11733555656507325805"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Well, maybe I can enjoy Steampunk after all. I definitely plan on continuing with this series.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I've been slow with reading the last month or two. This book was no different. That's not it's fault though. I found it every enjoyable the whole way.<br/><br/>When I did finally have some time over this holiday weekend to read, instead of reading 75-100 pages like I had planned, I ended up reading nearly half the book in one sitting.<br/><br/>Steampunk has never really appealed to me. I h</span>
  <span id="freeText11733555656507325805" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Well, maybe I can enjoy Steampunk after all. I definitely plan on continuing with this series.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I've been slow with reading the last month or two. This book was no different. That's not it's fault though. I found it every enjoyable the whole way.<br /><br />When I did finally have some time over this holiday weekend to read, instead of reading 75-100 pages like I had planned, I ended up reading nearly half the book in one sitting.<br /><br />Steampunk has never really appealed to me. I haven't read a lot of it as a result. The little I have read was alright, but didn't leave me itching to read more.<br /><br />This one got added to the pile because someone (I forget who now) said it's a bit like Firefly or the Expanse books. It's really not though. The only real similarity with either series is that it's about a crew aboard a ship who aren't loyal to anyone but themselves. In some ways this makes it like Cowboy Bebop, but I find those characters instantly a lot more likeable than these.<br /><br />And in this book, themselves is not so much each other as to their own self. I didn't like the captain (or most of the crew for that matter) very much at the start. They grew on me as the book went on.<br /><br />The characters are all fairly interesting and different enough, just not the sort of people I'd want to hang around with. All of them have things in their past they'd like to keep there. The Ketty Jay is the perfect place for that. You don't ask about my past, and I won't ask about yours.<br /><br />So more a crew full of strangers all running from their past. Darian Frey is no James Holden, and or even a Malcolm Reynolds. He only cares about his ship, and not the people on it.<br /><br />This book serves like an origin story of sorts. You not only meet the characters and learn of their past, but things end in a lot different place than when it starts. It was a fun ride to get there too.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to checking out the rest of this series when I have more time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11733555656507325805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_227265964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227265964" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227265964?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227265964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4488186239551074929">Full praise for this book from me. Not so much for some intrinsic or objective artistic value, but for the fun I've had reading it.<br/>The story is probably one we've heard numerous time before. A group of down of their luck misfits and outcasts try to make a living at the edge of the civilized world, playing a game of risk in a dangerous environment and stepping on the wrong side of the law every so often. We already had The Argonauts, some of the Knights of the Round Table, The Elizabethan private</span>
  <span id="freeText4488186239551074929" style="display:none">Full praise for this book from me. Not so much for some intrinsic or objective artistic value, but for the fun I've had reading it.<br />The story is probably one we've heard numerous time before. A group of down of their luck misfits and outcasts try to make a living at the edge of the civilized world, playing a game of risk in a dangerous environment and stepping on the wrong side of the law every so often. We already had The Argonauts, some of the Knights of the Round Table, The Elizabethan privateers so vividly portayed by Errol Flynn or John Barrymore, the Corsairs of the Carribean and the Outlaws of the Wild West. more recently we had Joss Wheddon and Firefly - the closest relative to the crew of the Ketty Jay.<br /><br />The story flows effortlessly from one mishap to another, from seedy airship ports to luxurious palaces or secluded monasteries. The worldbuilding is top notch, with many civilizations, a rich history and complex political / military conflicts. The geography is seen mostly from the air - steep mountains, misty valleys, frozen outposts or lush islands.<br /><br />We get to know the Origin story of each member of the crew, brought together by an inability to conform to the rules of society or simply by personal vices or bad luck. They are a spirited bunch, fond of hard liquor and coarse humor, independent spirits trying to forge a team and learn responsibility for their action. Here is where the story raises above mere entertainment, clicheed plot twists and special effects thrills.<br />One special note of praise from me to Mr Wooding for managing to convey the danger and the ruthlessness of the underworld without falling into the recent fad of excessive cussing or blood squirts. His characters still believe in redemption and adventure for the sake of it.<br /><br />looking forward to the next two Ketty Jay books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4488186239551074929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1888745468931229563">Retribution Falls took me on a journey where I was continually required to reevaluate everything-- from the story itself, the world in which it takes place, and not the least, the characters. It was complex, intriguing, and ultimately very enjoyable.<br/><br/>Reviewed for Bitten By books. <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bittenbybooks.com'>http://bittenbybooks.com</a>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15627089197431455148">Pure fun; and do not be fooled by the pulp-like presentation of the novel with chapters with headings a la Jules Verne, since the novel is thoroughly modern in tone and content, partly ironic, partly serious.<br/><br/>I laughed out loud many, many times, but there is a lot of heartbreak and tragedy.<br/><br/>A crew of misfits led by one Darian Frey who seems to attract the attention of beautiful rich girls once too many for his own good is scrapping a living as airship smugglers and occasional pirates. Kind of bott</span>
  <span id="freeText15627089197431455148" style="display:none">Pure fun; and do not be fooled by the pulp-like presentation of the novel with chapters with headings a la Jules Verne, since the novel is thoroughly modern in tone and content, partly ironic, partly serious.<br /><br />I laughed out loud many, many times, but there is a lot of heartbreak and tragedy.<br /><br />A crew of misfits led by one Darian Frey who seems to attract the attention of beautiful rich girls once too many for his own good is scrapping a living as airship smugglers and occasional pirates. Kind of bottom feeders in the underworld, but Darian and his crew are happy that way, or to be more precise they are just content to try and survive a day at a time and forget the past...<br /><br />But when a nasty job needs to be done, no survivors required, someone hires the "right" captain with the right "hook". <br /><br />Of course Darian Frey does the job, which is not quite what he expected either, but his crew are better than even they knew, so they inconveniently survive; however a large reward with an accurate wanted Frey poster may finally eliminate the inconvenience especially when fearsome bounty hunter Trinica Dracken who has a personal interest in the matter gets involved.<br /><br />But being cornered and with no seeming escape possible is just what may finally rouse Frey and his crew from their personal mistakes and tragedies induced apathy and the plotters may just regret having staked the Ketty Jay crew as a scapegoat...<br /><br />Highly, highly recommended and one of the most pure fun novels I read in a long time</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575085169" href="/book/show/6854741-retribution-falls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/978552-cathy?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1452264155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3095310825883348504">This was supposed to be fast-paced action. It's not bad, but taking into account some of the whiplash-inducing UF I have read in the last few years, this is pretty average. The blurb sounds interesting, the cover is really nice. But it took me a week to slog through the first 100 pages, as I could simply not build up any interest in the story or the charactes.<br/><br/>We have the mischievous criminal with a presumabely good heart and his band of misfits. A new crew member joins and gives us the outside v</span>
  <span id="freeText3095310825883348504" style="display:none">This was supposed to be fast-paced action. It's not bad, but taking into account some of the whiplash-inducing UF I have read in the last few years, this is pretty average. The blurb sounds interesting, the cover is really nice. But it took me a week to slog through the first 100 pages, as I could simply not build up any interest in the story or the charactes.<br /><br />We have the mischievous criminal with a presumabely good heart and his band of misfits. A new crew member joins and gives us the outside view, also not a new idea. A job goes wrong and all of a sudden they are at the top of the most-wanted list. To get out of this, they have to find the real culprit in the whole scheme. <br /><br />I like the writing style. Very visual. The characters and the world-building are not bad either. But I don't care, I don't like any of the protagonists and I am bored. Probably another case of "It's not you, it's me..."<br /><br />DNF at page 94, beginning of Chapter 11.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_377999655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/377999655" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/377999655?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575085169" href="/book/show/6854741-retribution-falls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer377999655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7546839717897614683">7.5/10<br/><br/>A fun, enjoyable romp which is a mix of fantasy, steampunk and action. As I've never seen Firefly I can't say this is like that series (but noticed that comparison in a number of other reviews) but I would class it as a mix of Red Dwarf and Lies of Locke Lamora. A ragtag crew gets given a hot tip on some loot they can easily take from another vessel, a tip that sounds too good to be true. Would you believe it but it's too good to be true, by a long shot. <br/><br/>There were plenty of positives in t</span>
  <span id="freeText7546839717897614683" style="display:none">7.5/10<br /><br />A fun, enjoyable romp which is a mix of fantasy, steampunk and action. As I've never seen Firefly I can't say this is like that series (but noticed that comparison in a number of other reviews) but I would class it as a mix of Red Dwarf and Lies of Locke Lamora. A ragtag crew gets given a hot tip on some loot they can easily take from another vessel, a tip that sounds too good to be true. Would you believe it but it's too good to be true, by a long shot. <br /><br />There were plenty of positives in this opener for the series; the world is easily introduced with no info dumps on the technology, magic or politics but it's nicely teased out throughout the book. The main trio of characters are well developed and go from independent travellers to trusted companions and the journey getting to that point is well written with plenty of backstory for these characters to properly flesh them out and make that progression seem worthwhile.<br /><br />The plot was a mixed bag, it wasn't anything brand spanking new but it did enough to push things along and get the crew interacting. At the start it was your basic double cross but halfway through the book it clicked a fair amount for me and I became more invested and wanted to find out more. I would also say that the character development aided this too.<br /><br />A minor complaint would be that some of the other crew members outside the top 3 were mere filler, nothing was really fleshed out here but I guess this was due to mainly concentrating on the leads and there is always more to come from the series. Also there was a direct steal from a Red Dwarf episode and one of their funnier scenes. <a href="https://m.youtube.com/watch?v=78RHJCQ0mXg" rel="nofollow noopener">Apologies on the clip, it's not my own but well worth getting the episode - S06E06</a><br /><br />Plenty of positives here and a fun light read with enough to keep me interested in the series going into the next book. I look forward to continuing these and seeing how the next story will continue with the characters now set in their ways amongst each other and their crew.<br /><br />If you like this try: "Lies of Locke Lamora" by Scott Lynch</span>
  <a data-text-id="7546839717897614683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37884491-priest-of-bones"><img alt="Priest of Bones (War for the Rose Throne, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1517589565l/37884491._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K7Av0xi63OXxODEzdbjbNcZ2LqawHzLU41vLGXo2ouMT5EuiD9nPlSAIdWHZ79sDw9M0EQajdEribZFND0hkLw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('11JLUKQuGqNkgmyBQvjKTNG+/LzBfhi70BPVRDtceKnvBi8hs00J07WyKNPur8p61BvmC3fCXiXRJY8QTiK+ZQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15344610950310469534">Chris Wooding grew up in a small town in Leicestershire, where not much of anything happened. So he started to write novels. He was sixteen when he completed his first. He had an agent by eighteen. By nineteen he had signed his first book deal. When he left university he began to write full-time, and he has been doing it professionally all his adult life.<br/><br/>Now thirty-nine, Chris has written over twe</span>
  <span id="freeText15344610950310469534" style="display:none">Chris Wooding grew up in a small town in Leicestershire, where not much of anything happened. So he started to write novels. He was sixteen when he completed his first. He had an agent by eighteen. By nineteen he had signed his first book deal. When he left university he began to write full-time, and he has been doing it professionally all his adult life.<br /><br />Now thirty-nine, Chris has written over twenty books, which have been translated into twenty languages, won various awards and been published around the world. He writes for film and television, and has several projects in development.<br /><br />Chris has travelled extensively round the world, having backpacked all over Europe and North America, Scandinavia, South East Asia, Japan and South Africa. He also lived in Madrid for a time. When he wasn’t travelling on his own, he spent his twenties touring with bands and seeing the UK and Europe from the back of a van.<br /><br />He also learned not so long ago that his family tree can be traced back to John Milton, author of Paradise Lost, which has no bearing on him whatsoever but it’s kind of interesting anyway.<br /><br />Chris lives in London.</span>
